  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_05e9534e-a8a6-457b-9f95-a7fe792b1504'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer3769735059840931207">At last, the costly and bitter war between the two Foundations had come to an end. The scientists of the First Foundation had proved victorious; and now they return to Hari Seldon's long-established plan to build a new Empire on the ruins of the old. But rumors persist that the Second Foundation is not destroyed after all—and that its still-defiant survivors are preparing </span>
  <span id="freeText3769735059840931207" style="display:none">At last, the costly and bitter war between the two Foundations had come to an end. The scientists of the First Foundation had proved victorious; and now they return to Hari Seldon's long-established plan to build a new Empire on the ruins of the old. But rumors persist that the Second Foundation is not destroyed after all—and that its still-defiant survivors are preparing their revenge. Now two exiled citizens of the Foundation—a renegade Councilman and a doddering historian—set out in search of the mythical planet Earth. . .and proof that the Second Foundation still exists.<br /><br />Meanwhile someone—or something—outside of both Foundations seems to be orchestrating events to suit its own ominous purpose. Soon representatives of both the First and Second Foundations will find themselves racing toward a mysterious world called Gaia and a final shocking destiny at the very end of the universe!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3769735059840931207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Yes, definitely. Asimov named his universe "The Foundation Universe". I think that the Eternals from Foundation's Edge are the computers that said "Le<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Yes, definitely. Asimov named his universe "The Foundation Universe". I think that the Eternals from Foundation's Edge are the computers that said "Let there be Light, and there was Light" and reversed Entropy and thus created humans again after the last one died out. I think that the events in the books take place in this new universe that's created in "The Last Question".<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

<div id="review_2355523898" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2355523898" />
    <a title="Luca Ambrosino" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53478239-luca-ambrosino"><img alt="Luca Ambrosino" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523134271p2/53478239.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2355523898?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luca Ambrosino" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luca Ambrosino" href="/user/show/53478239-luca-ambrosino">Luca Ambrosino</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788804398165" href="/book/show/8881365-l-orlo-della-fondazione">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2355523898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17592994816897375904">English (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76683.Foundation_s_Edge__Foundation__4_' title='Foundation's Edge (Foundation #4) by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>Foundation's Edge</a>)/ Italiano<br/><br/><blockquote>«The First Galactic Empire was falling. It had been decaying and breaking down for centuries and only one man fully realized that fact. He was Han Seldon, the last great scientist of the First Empire, and it was he who perfected psychohistory-the science of human behavior reduced to mathematical equations»</blockquote><p>The story so far: a large part of the galaxy is under is controlled by the Foundation, and the Seldon Plan, in place for 500 years, is perfectly progressing</p></span>
  <span id="freeText17592994816897375904" style="display:none">English (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76683.Foundation_s_Edge__Foundation__4_" title="Foundation's Edge (Foundation #4) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation's Edge</a>)/ Italiano<br><br><blockquote>«The First Galactic Empire was falling. It had been decaying and breaking down for centuries and only one man fully realized that fact. He was Han Seldon, the last great scientist of the First Empire, and it was he who perfected psychohistory-the science of human behavior reduced to mathematical equations»</blockquote><p>The story so far: a large part of the galaxy is under is controlled by the Foundation, and the Seldon Plan, in place for 500 years, is perfectly progressing. So perfectly, enough to raise doubts about its existence...</p><p>Here we come to chapter four of the Foundation series (if we do not consider also two preludes, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30013.Prelude_to_Foundation" title="Prelude to Foundation by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Prelude to Foundation</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76679.Forward_the_Foundation__Foundation_Prequel__2_" title="Forward the Foundation (Foundation Prequel #2) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Forward the Foundation</a>, and one sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29582.Foundation_and_Earth__Foundation__5_" title="Foundation and Earth (Foundation #5) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation and Earth</a>). And we come probably to the best among these four, written 30 years later after the publication of the previous three books. A more mature <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov" title="Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Isaac Asimov</a> distributes science-fiction ideas about the colonization of the universe left, right and centre, increasingly persuasive and tantalizing. The sensation that in the distant future described by Asimov the loop will be closed is strong now. Only one more book. We can do that.</p><p>Vote: 8</p><p>
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522014459i/25274252._SX540_.jpg" width="420" height="315" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
</p><blockquote>«Il Primo Impero Galattico stava crollando. Erano secoli che si stava sgretolando e disfacendo, e solo un uomo si rendeva pienamente conto della cosa. Quell'uomo era Hari Seldon, l'ultimo grande scienziato del Primo Impero. Era stato lui a perfezionare la psicostoria, ovvero la scienza del comportamento umano espressa in equazioni matematiche»</blockquote><p>La situazione finora: la Fondazione controlla oramai buona parte della Galassia, ed il Piano Seldon, in atto da 500 anni, procede perfettamente. Troppo perfettamente, tanto da generare dubbi sulla sua stessa esistenza...</p><p>Giungiamo al quarto capitolo del ciclo della Fondazione (se non contiamo anche i due preludi, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10314009.Preludio_alla_Fondazione" title="Preludio alla Fondazione by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Preludio alla Fondazione</a> e <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9646838.Fondazione_Anno_Zero" title="Fondazione Anno Zero by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Fondazione Anno Zero</a>, e il sequel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9646840.Fondazione_e_Terra" title="Fondazione e Terra by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Fondazione e Terra</a>). E giungiamo probabilmente al migliore dei quattro, non a caso scritto ben trent'anni dopo la pubblicazione dei primi tre. Un <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov" title="Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Isaac Asimov</a> più maturo, che distribuisce a destra e a manca fantascientifiche teorie di colonizzazione dell'Universo sempre più convincenti e stuzzicanti. La sensazione che nel lontano futuro descritto da Asimov si sta per chiudere il cerchio in maniera decisiva è forte. Manca un solo libro. Ce la possiamo fare.</p><p>Voto: 8</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="17592994816897375904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1438578805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4285395859566741780">Foundation's Edge (Foundation (Publication Order) #4), Isaac Asimov<br/> <br/>Foundation's Edge (1982) is a science fiction novel by American writer Isaac Asimov, the fourth book in the Foundation Series. <br/><br/>It was written more than thirty years after the stories of the original Foundation trilogy, due to years of pressure by fans and editors on Asimov to write another, and, according to Asimov himself, the amount of the payment offered by the publisher. <br/><br/>It was his first novel to ever land on The New York Ti</span>
  <span id="freeText4285395859566741780" style="display:none">Foundation's Edge (Foundation (Publication Order) #4), Isaac Asimov<br /> <br />Foundation's Edge (1982) is a science fiction novel by American writer Isaac Asimov, the fourth book in the Foundation Series. <br /><br />It was written more than thirty years after the stories of the original Foundation trilogy, due to years of pressure by fans and editors on Asimov to write another, and, according to Asimov himself, the amount of the payment offered by the publisher. <br /><br />It was his first novel to ever land on The New York Times best-seller list, after 262 books and 44 years of writing. Foundation's Edge won both the Hugo Award for Best Novel in 1983 and the Locus Award for Best Science Fiction Novel in 1983, and was nominated for the Nebula Award for Best Novel in 1982.<br /><br />Five hundred years after the establishment of the Foundation, the Mayor of Terminus, Harla Branno, is basking in a political glow, her policies having been vindicated by the recent successful resolution of a Seldon Crisis. Golan Trevize, a former officer of the Navy and now a member of Council, believes the Second Foundation (which is almost universally thought to be extinct) still exists and is controlling events. <br /><br />He attempts to question the continued existence of the Seldon Plan during a Council session and Branno has him arrested on a charge of treason. Branno also believes that the Second Foundation still exists and is in control, but she cannot admit it publicly for political reasons, and treats that as a state secret, hence her alarm and her swift action.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: سال 1995میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: لبه بنیاد کهکشانی؛ نویسنده: آیزاک آسیموف؛ مترجم: پیمان اسماعیلیان خامنه؛ تهران، بنیاد مستضعفان و جانبازان، 1373، در 520ص، موضوع داستانهای علمی تخیلی از نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 20م<br /><br />چهارصد و نود و هشت سال از هنگام پیدایش بنیاد اول میگذرد؛ بنیاد در اوج قدرت خود است، اما یک نفر هست که به ظاهر امر اکتفا نمیکند<br /><br />سری بنیاد نام مجموعه ‌ای هفت جلدی از آیزاک آسیموف است که نامدارترین سری علمی-تخیلی خوانده شده‌ است؛ داستان این مجموعه به ترتیب زمان انتشار پیش نمی‌رود، بلکه «آسیموف» نخست جلدهای سوم (بنیاد)، جلد چهارم (بنیاد و امپراطوری) و جلد پنجم (بنیاد دوم) را نوشتند؛ و سپس با وقفه ‌ای طولانی مدت، و با پافشاری خوانشگران، جلد ششم (لبه بنیاد) و جلد هفتم (بنیاد و زمین) را به آنها افزودند؛ پس از آن با وقفه ‌ای نسبتاً طولانی جلد نخست سری با عنوان (سرآغاز بنیاد) و در نهایت نیز اندکی پیش از درگذشتشان جلد دوم (پیشبرد بنیاد) را نوشته اند؛ «آسیموف» داستان‌های بلند و کوتاه بسیاری نگاشته ‌است و می‌توان گفت، مهم‌ترین آثار ایشان، کتاب‌ها و داستان‌هایی هستند، که به نام «سری بنیاد» شناخته می‌شوند؛ کتاب‌های اصلی بنیاد به ترتیب خط داستانی عبارتند از: «سرآغاز بنیاد کهکشانی»؛ «پیشبرد بنیاد کهکشانی»؛ «بنیاد (ظهور امپراطوری کهکشان‌ها در ترجمهٔ فارسی)»؛ «بنیاد و امپراطوری (جنگ امپراطوری کهکشان‌ها در ترجمهٔ فارسی)»؛ «بنیاد دوم (سقوط امپراطوری کهکشان‌ها در ترجمهٔ فارسی)»؛ «لبه بنیاد»؛<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 26/06/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_986605933" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/986605933" />
    <a title="Apatt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt"><img alt="Apatt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/986605933?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apatt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apatt" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt">Apatt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer986605933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2746478729185072371">First published in 1982 almost 30 years after the last volume of the iconic original Foundation Trilogy, namely <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29580.Second_Foundation__Foundation___3_' title='Second Foundation (Foundation, #3) by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>Second Foundation</a>, I was skeptical that Asimov would be able to maintain his mojo post the Golden Age of Science Fiction when he was publishing his most iconic sci-fi stories and novels. Of his 80s books I only read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41810.The_Robots_of_Dawn__Robot___3_' title='The Robots of Dawn (Robot, #3) by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Robots of Dawn</a> which I thought was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/800880537' rel='nofollow noopener'>quite good</a> but not in the same league as his 50s robot novels <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41811.The_Caves_of_Steel__Robot___1_' title='The Caves of Steel (Robot, #1) by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Caves of Steel</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30016.The_Naked_Sun__Robot___2_' title='The Naked Sun (Robot, #2) by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Naked Sun</a>. Still, I liked it enough to rekin</span>
  <span id="freeText2746478729185072371" style="display:none">First published in 1982 almost 30 years after the last volume of the iconic original Foundation Trilogy, namely <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29580.Second_Foundation__Foundation___3_" title="Second Foundation (Foundation, #3) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Second Foundation</a>, I was skeptical that Asimov would be able to maintain his mojo post the Golden Age of Science Fiction when he was publishing his most iconic sci-fi stories and novels. Of his 80s books I only read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41810.The_Robots_of_Dawn__Robot___3_" title="The Robots of Dawn (Robot, #3) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">The Robots of Dawn</a> which I thought was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/800880537" rel="nofollow noopener">quite good</a> but not in the same league as his 50s robot novels <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41811.The_Caves_of_Steel__Robot___1_" title="The Caves of Steel (Robot, #1) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">The Caves of Steel</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30016.The_Naked_Sun__Robot___2_" title="The Naked Sun (Robot, #2) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">The Naked Sun</a>. Still, I liked it enough to rekindle my interest in the Foundation series of which I have only read the original trilogy in my teens. For some reason I neglected the series from the 4th volume onwards and to catch up I did not want to simply dive into it as it was decades ago since I read the previous books and I have gotten most of the background details. So I reread the trilogy a couple of months ago and enjoyed it very much in spite of already knowing the major plot twists. The Foundation saga remains quite potent after all these years.<br><br><i>Foundation's Edge</i> is the 4th volume I speak of. It is set 500 years after the establishment of the Foundation. <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seldon_Plan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Seldon Plan</a> is going swimmingly and the First Foundation is at the peak of its strength having dominated all the neighboring planets through its superior technology and military might. The people of the Foundation believe that the threat from the mind controlling Second Foundation has been eliminated and there is now only one Foundation, theirs. Alas someone always shows up to rock the boat otherwise we would not have much of a story. Enters one Golan Trevize, a Council member and an original thinker; a dangerous combination. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469081073i/19777261._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>It occurs to Trevize that the Seldon Plan has been going too well of late and there is surely something wrong when things are just too right. It is unnatural for things to always go according to plan, some deviations must occur. Trevize believes this is an indication that the Foundation is being surreptitiously controlled by puppet masters from the dreaded Second Foundation who will ensure the Seldon Plan reaches fruition and then step in as lord and masters. Voicing such a controversial idea turns out to be unwise as he is summarily kicked off the planet Terminus (home of the Foundation) with a secret mission to locate the Second Foundation in order for the First to do away with them once and for all. Many surprises ensue.<br><br>In spite of not being action packed as such, I find <i>Foundation's Edge</i> to be a gripping page-turner. The plot tends to move through dialogue rather than narration. Every page seems to be stuffed with dialogue as characters are always discussing or arguing about something. The climax is also played through dialogue. This is a surprisingly effective method of storytelling as the book is never dull. Asimov writes reasonably good dialogue, but his characters do have a tendency to belabor their points at times. <br><br>Asimov’s major strengths are his epic ideas, world building and plot; these are the reason he is one of the most popular sci-fi authors of all time (possibly <i>the</i> most popular). His world building here is better than ever, I particularly love the telepathic society and culture of the Second Foundation on Trantor and the strange people of Gaia. It is also lovely to see the robots and their “Three Laws” worked into the Foundation universe, plus a clever explanation for the absence of aliens in the Foundation universe.<br><br>Asimov is often criticized for his utilitarian prose and thin characters (the same criticisms leveled toward most Golden Age authors). While he was no Dickens or Oscar Wilde in term of prose, characterization and dialogue I find these criticisms a little unfair. His prose is not extraordinary, but it is uncluttered and very readable, it is never clumsy or semi-literate; he never insults the readers’ intelligence. His dialogue is often full of amusing witty banter and sardonic remarks. As for his characters, while some of the supporting characters are indeed flat his central characters and protagonists are often memorable. After decades away from his books I still remember very well Hari Seldon, The Mule, Susan Calvin (from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41804.I__Robot__Robot___0_1_" title="I, Robot (Robot, #0.1) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">I Robot</a>), Elijah Baley and R. Daneel Olivaw (from several robot novels). As for <i>Foundation's Edge</i>'s characters, Golan Trevize, and several lead characters are quite vivid and memorable also. In contrast I can not remember a single character from Arthur C. Clarke’s books (except Hal 9000 and Dave Bowman); no disrespect to Sir Arthur though, he has his own brand of greatness. <br><br>The climax of <i>Foundation's Edge</i> is just wonderful and the epilogue leads nicely to the next book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29582.Foundation_and_Earth__Foundation___5_" title="Foundation and Earth (Foundation, #5) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation and Earth</a>. Asimov always seems to enjoy telling his Foundation stories tremendously and his enjoyment is infectious. Can’t wait!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2746478729185072371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/326275104" />
    <a title="Clouds" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds"><img alt="Clouds" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514641128p2/9374686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/326275104?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clouds" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clouds" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds">Clouds</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780606192750" href="/book/show/3934980-foundation-s-edge">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=locus-sci-fi">locus-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=science-fiction-series">science-fiction-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=hugo">hugo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=pub-1980s">pub-1980s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer326275104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12650466333355729109"><a href='http://www.theaceofclouds.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317319i/689370.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>Christmas 2010: I realised that I had got stuck in a rut. I was re-reading old favourites again and again, waiting for a few trusted authors to release new works. Something had to be done.<br/><br/>On the spur of the moment I set myself a challenge, to read every book to have won the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=2' rel='nofollow noopener'>Locus Sci-Fi</a> award. That’s 35 books, 6 of which I’d previously read, leaving 29 titles by 14 authors who were new to me.<br/><br/>While working through this reading list I got married, went on my honeymoon, switched career and beca</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12650466333355729109" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.theaceofclouds.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317319i/689370.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Christmas 2010: I realised that I had got stuck in a rut. I was re-reading old favourites again and again, waiting for a few trusted authors to release new works. Something had to be done.<br><br>On the spur of the moment I set myself a challenge, to read every book to have won the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=2" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus Sci-Fi</a> award. That’s 35 books, 6 of which I’d previously read, leaving 29 titles by 14 authors who were new to me.<br><br>While working through this reading list I got married, went on my honeymoon, switched career and became a father. As such these stories became imprinted on my memory as the soundtrack to the happiest period in my life (so far).</b><br><br><i>
  <b>
    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3934980-foundation-s-edge" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation’s Edge</a>
  </b>
</i> won the Locus Sci-Fi award in 1983, finishing ahead of <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1018538.Golden_Torc" rel="nofollow noopener">The Golden Torc</a>
</i> (sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/378639.The_Many_Coloured_Land" rel="nofollow noopener">the previous year’s winner</a>), <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/70539.2010" rel="nofollow noopener">2010</a>
</i> (the sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7779.Arthur_C_Clarke" rel="nofollow noopener">Arthur C Clarke</a>’s classic <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/70535.2001" rel="nofollow noopener">2001</a>
</i>) and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/653711.Crystal_Singer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crystal Singer</a>
</i> (the first in what, my wife and Mother assure me, is a fine <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Ann McCaffrey</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43910-crystal-singer" rel="nofollow noopener">trilogy</a>) to name just three.<br><br>I’ve read the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43939-foundation" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation series</a> twice in my life, and <i>
  <b>
    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3934980-foundation-s-edge" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation’s Edge</a>
  </b>
</i> was one of the six winning books I had previously read before I began my Locus Quest.<br><br>The first time I read the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43939-foundation" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation series</a> as an awe-struck pre-teen, I’d have instantly given the whole series a 5-star review: it was a story that became a foundation stone (excuse the pun) of my love for sci-fi. <br><br>Let's get this out of the way: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Asimov</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43939-foundation" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation series</a> is required reading for anyone with more than a passing interest in science fiction. If you've not read it yet, put it on your list!<br><br>Returning to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Asimov</a> in my mid twenties I was expecting to be disappointed. Some issues are unavoidable – much of the characterisation is shallow and doesn’t develop far and there series as a whole tends to repeat plot devices with surface variations – but overall I was pleasantly surprised. <br><br>Asimov tends to remind me <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/880695.H_G_Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">H.G. Wells</a>. That may sound extreme considering <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2493.The_Time_Machine" rel="nofollow noopener">The Time Machine</a>
</i> was written in the 1890s while <i>
  <b>
    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3934980-foundation-s-edge" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation’s Edge</a>
  </b>
</i> was released in the 1980s, but the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43939-foundation" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation series</a> was conceived back in the 50s. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/880695.H_G_Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">Wells</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Asimov</a> may represent the best of pre-WW1 and post-WW2 sci-fi, but their formative cultures have more in common with each other than post-2012 audiences.<br><br>To me, their stories are now are charming combination of dated ideals and visionary speculation. <br><br>This is one of the few <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43939-foundation-chronological-order" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation</a> novels which can stand alone, so I can heartily recommend it to all - not just fans of the series.<br><br>I’m no longer blown away as I once was, but it’s still a very enjoyable read!<br><br><b>After this I read: </b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/326279832" rel="nofollow noopener">Ilium</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12650466333355729109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2020752584" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2020752584" />
    <a title="Adrian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22809267-adrian"><img alt="Adrian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484242635p2/22809267.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2020752584?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adrian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adrian" href="/user/show/22809267-adrian">Adrian</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780586058398" href="/book/show/509829.Foundation_s_Edge">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22809267-adrian?shelf=read-again">read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22809267-adrian?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22809267-adrian?shelf=zz-owned-books">zz-owned-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2020752584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5352783047757731869">Although written much later than the original Foundation trilogy, this book in my opinion is on a par with them. Not only is it a great story, well written as ever by Asimov, but after having read the Foundation novels, the Robot novels and the Empire novels (some many times), you realise how cleverly this book starts to bring everything together the way Asimov intended.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1777788373" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1777788373" />
    <a title="Denisse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8759700-denisse"><img alt="Denisse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606102662p2/8759700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1777788373?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denisse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denisse" href="/user/show/8759700-denisse">Denisse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1777788373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10110962567795333988">Asimov surrounds me everytime I read his books. This time he worked more on the characters and their interactions, which made the book even more fluent to enjoy. The writing style is still very simple, so even when the plot gets dense it doesn't bother and <b>everything Asimov has to say about the Universe, the human race, our minds as a group or a single person is so fascinated to me</b>. A very special book about balance, our decisions and how important they are. Second favorite behind Foundation. I </span>
  <span id="freeText10110962567795333988" style="display:none">Asimov surrounds me everytime I read his books. This time he worked more on the characters and their interactions, which made the book even more fluent to enjoy. The writing style is still very simple, so even when the plot gets dense it doesn't bother and <b>everything Asimov has to say about the Universe, the human race, our minds as a group or a single person is so fascinated to me</b>. A very special book about balance, our decisions and how important they are. Second favorite behind Foundation. I really enjoyed this continuation. <br /><br /><br /><b>
  <i>En una epoca extraña e imprevisible, nos aferrramos con miedo al pasado.</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Lo más page-turner de Asimov que he leído hasta ahora.</b> La trilogía de la Fundación original es más seria, por decirlo de un modo, con Los Limites de la Fundación se divierte más sin dejar su estilo y sin arriesgar la trama. Hay personajes más activos, diálogos más fluidos y un misterio más interesante. Digamos que solo deja de meterse tanto con los problemas sociales y nos adentramos más a una aventura espacial mientras el Plan de Hari Seldon está a mitad de camino.<br /><br />Como siempre, este Plan se ve amenazado por alguna disputa y/o pensamiento desviado y ahora para prevenir la catástrofe se debe enderezar el camino. Y como siempre, <b>la resolución final es contundente, imaginativa e ingeniosa al mismo tiempo, lo que hace del libro una experiencia increíble de forma redonda.</b> <br /><br /><i>
  <b>Lo unico que debe hacer es mirarse atentamente a si mismo y entendera a todos los demas.</b>
</i><br /><br />Otro gran detalle son las dos grandes referencias a otros libros del autor, te hablan sobre el pasado prehistórico del Primer Imperio Galáctico y te pica la curiosidad por leer esos otros volúmenes <s>de los cuales ya tengo uno yei!</s><br /><br />En general, esta cuarta entrega de la serie trata más acerca de lo que escapa a ambas Fundaciones, su razón de ser y su papel en la historia. <b>Ha sido muy interesante y te deja con muchas ganas de leer Fundación y Tierra</b>...es una pena que no lo encontrara en la Feria del Libro. Espero lo traigan pronto. Recomendado para quienes disfrutaron la trilogía principal.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Si hubieramos esperado hasta que la seguridad fuese doble y triple y cuadruple e infinitamente grande, habriamos esperado siempre. </i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10110962567795333988" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_19970419" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/19970419" />
    <a title="ttrygve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/277970-ttrygve"><img alt="ttrygve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1267222111p2/277970.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/19970419?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ttrygve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ttrygve" href="/user/show/277970-ttrygve">ttrygve</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer19970419&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19970419" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17945907561643439420">This was, like its predecessors, an enjoyable story. I enjoyed the premise for it, the pacing, and even the characterization is very much improved over the earlier Foundation novels (however little that may be saying).<br/><br/>But I cannot review this book without spoiling it. So read no further if that bothers you.<br/><br/>The real shortcoming is that Asimov abandons (at the very end) the first two foundations to have yet a third organization secretly pull strings from behind a curtain. I get that they're benevo</span>
  <span id="freeText17945907561643439420" style="display:none">This was, like its predecessors, an enjoyable story. I enjoyed the premise for it, the pacing, and even the characterization is very much improved over the earlier Foundation novels (however little that may be saying).<br /><br />But I cannot review this book without spoiling it. So read no further if that bothers you.<br /><br />The real shortcoming is that Asimov abandons (at the very end) the first two foundations to have yet a third organization secretly pull strings from behind a curtain. I get that they're benevolent, that's fine, but Asimov spent the first three books building up the predictive powers of psychohistory as thoroughly grounded in scientific fact and experimentation, and vetted and improved upon by the Second Foundation, only to tear it down in this book and say -- without a bit of explanation -- that it wasn't good enough to account for the growth rate of technology, despite the fact that that's a big part of what it had been designed specifically to do and had done just fine at thus far.<br /><br />But now we end up with yet a *third* organization working to construct a new second empire. This one, like the second, also operates in secrecy in order to achieve its goals, and so *again* Asimov comes back to ignorance as a key to solving problems created by knowledge, and that just seems like a huge betrayal of the principles he seems to be trying to embrace. He seems to have this split desire to deify science and the pursuit of knowledge in general most of the time, while embracing ignorance at other times. It's just too incongruent, in that regard.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17945907561643439420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_177422420" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177422420" />
    <a title="Jan-Maat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5617661-jan-maat"><img alt="Jan-Maat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407579968p2/5617661.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177422420?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jan-Maat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jan-Maat" href="/user/show/5617661-jan-maat">Jan-Maat</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5617661-jan-maat?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5617661-jan-maat?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5617661-jan-maat?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5617661-jan-maat?shelf=usa">usa</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177422420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14713602808944895270">Sort of brick-like sequel to the earlier Foundation books. The sheer bulk of the book testifies to the difference in publishing between when Azimov wrote his original stories - mostly first printed in magazines and later released as books and as a result far shorter. But this was not all that had changed, the story testifies to a change in Azimov's thinking and vision. The original stories were the product of post WWII USA there is an uncomplicated optimism about technology and in the values of </span>
  <span id="freeText14713602808944895270" style="display:none">Sort of brick-like sequel to the earlier Foundation books. The sheer bulk of the book testifies to the difference in publishing between when Azimov wrote his original stories - mostly first printed in magazines and later released as books and as a result far shorter. But this was not all that had changed, the story testifies to a change in Azimov's thinking and vision. The original stories were the product of post WWII USA there is an uncomplicated optimism about technology and in the values of the USA, the far future as a result is the 1950s writ large with a generous splash of Gibbons' <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19400.The_Decline_and_Fall_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="The Decline and Fall of the Roman Empire by Edward Gibbon" rel="nofollow noopener">Decline and Fall of the Roman Empire</a>, a degree of pessimism as the necessary sauce to sharpen the faith in those fundamental values.<br /><br />This book takes the Foundation idea in a slightly different direction by introducing a factor and the possibility of a factor outside of the original psychohistorical calculations made by Seldon. Which rather renders the original stories superfluous. The drive of late Azimov to completeness and neatness, tying all of his stories together into one superbundle is accomplished at the cost of the integrity and cleverness of those original stories from the 40s and 50s. One can read and enjoy this book and the one that comes after it and as a pair they serve to tie the Foundation series back to the Bailey/robot books. <br /><br />More seriously Azimov's solutions in the 1980s are revealed to be thoroughly collectivist, he had moved a long way from his starting point.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14713602808944895270" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2151431495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2151431495" />
    <a title="Michael Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72416163-michael-campbell"><img alt="Michael Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583366142p2/72416163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2151431495?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Campbell" href="/user/show/72416163-michael-campbell">Michael Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2151431495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8175436714831918780">For the past four years, I've been reading one Foundation book a year. I'm not entirely sure why that is; you would imagine I'd forget a lot of what I read in the year between books. However, every time I come back to this series, it feels like I read the previous book only yesterday. <br/><br/>At first I was skeptical of this one. I read that he wrote this one decades after the third installment and was worried this was written just as a bit of fan service. If that's true, this is the highest quality fan</span>
  <span id="freeText8175436714831918780" style="display:none">For the past four years, I've been reading one Foundation book a year. I'm not entirely sure why that is; you would imagine I'd forget a lot of what I read in the year between books. However, every time I come back to this series, it feels like I read the previous book only yesterday. <br /><br />At first I was skeptical of this one. I read that he wrote this one decades after the third installment and was worried this was written just as a bit of fan service. If that's true, this is the highest quality fan service I've ever read.<br /><br />Out of the four I've read so far, this is the one that follows more of the standard novel format the most. One set of characters throughout the novel and doesn't time skip a generation or two at any point. I really enjoyed the change of pace, because what a brilliant cast he put into this novel!<br /><br />The plot twists were abundant and kept me guessing right up until the end. In fact, I'm still guessing after having read it. I wish I'd have read more of his novels before reading this, because I know he ties up several series with this book. Even without having read the other series, it felt fluid and well done. <br /><br />Isaac Asimov is without a doubt, my favorite Hard Science Fiction author. Every book I read by him cements that further. A few years ago, I'd have said Frank Herbert because of the extent to which Dune blew my mind. That series dwindled immediately after the first installment. All of the Foundation books have been as good, if not better than the first. I might have to read the next Foundation book this year even!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8175436714831918780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2823068476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13231006230685905827">16/5 - Yay! Finally an Asimov that I looked forward to picking up every night (reading before bed). I thought this was outstanding compared to <i>Foundation</i> and <i>Foundation and Empire</i>. Asimov's dialogue was still awkward, but in the 29 years between the publication of <i>Second Foundation</i> and this book Asimov certainly improved his skills in writing believable dialogue for his characters. Sometimes it felt like Trevize, or his travelling partner Janov Pelorat, were repeating their explanation of the si</span>
  <span id="freeText13231006230685905827" style="display:none">16/5 - Yay! Finally an Asimov that I looked forward to picking up every night (reading before bed). I thought this was outstanding compared to <i>Foundation</i> and <i>Foundation and Empire</i>. Asimov's dialogue was still awkward, but in the 29 years between the publication of <i>Second Foundation</i> and this book Asimov certainly improved his skills in writing believable dialogue for his characters. Sometimes it felt like Trevize, or his travelling partner Janov Pelorat, were repeating their explanation of the situation needlessly (and annoyingly), but I never found myself bored by the plot or the prose. The relationship between Trevize and Pelorat was what made the book for me. The hunt for the Second Foundation would not have been so enjoyable (for them trapped together on a not humongous spaceship for weeks, or me) if these characters hadn't interacted so well with each other. When I finished this I was actually looking forward to starting <i>Foundation and Earth</i> immediately.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13231006230685905827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_502233503" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/502233503" />
    <a title="David (דוד) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5431286-david"><img alt="David (דוד) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604688233p2/5431286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/502233503?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David (דוד) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="David (דוד) " href="/user/show/5431286-david">David (דוד) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345308986" href="/book/show/414856.Foundation_s_Edge">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who has read The Original Foundation Trilogy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5431286-david?shelf=owned-read">owned-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5431286-david?shelf=american-writing">american-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5431286-david?shelf=sf-space-opera">sf-space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5431286-david?shelf=political-sf">political-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5431286-david?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5431286-david?shelf=hard-sf">hard-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5431286-david?shelf=issac-asimov">issac-asimov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5431286-david?shelf=to-be-read-in-this-life-done">to-be-read-in-this-life-done</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5431286-david?shelf=jewish-writers">jewish-writers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5431286-david?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer502233503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer700009627211437667">4.5 Stars<br/>Definitely a better read than the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46654.The_Foundation_Trilogy__Foundation___1_3_' title='The Foundation Trilogy (Foundation, #1-3) by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Foundation Trilogy</a>, as some friends had suggested. :)<br/><br/>Having written this much later in life (early 1980s, 32 years after the publication of the previous Foundation book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29580.Second_Foundation__Foundation__3_' title='Second Foundation (Foundation #3) by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>Second Foundation</a>), Asimov's writing style seems to have had improved than from the 1950s. The book won the Hugo Award for best novel and the Locus Award for Best Science Fiction Novel in 1983. Although the book is self-contained, the story in this book is a continuation to the origi</span>
  <span id="freeText700009627211437667" style="display:none">4.5 Stars<br />Definitely a better read than the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46654.The_Foundation_Trilogy__Foundation___1_3_" title="The Foundation Trilogy (Foundation, #1-3) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">The Foundation Trilogy</a>, as some friends had suggested. :)<br /><br />Having written this much later in life (early 1980s, 32 years after the publication of the previous Foundation book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29580.Second_Foundation__Foundation__3_" title="Second Foundation (Foundation #3) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Second Foundation</a>), Asimov's writing style seems to have had improved than from the 1950s. The book won the Hugo Award for best novel and the Locus Award for Best Science Fiction Novel in 1983. Although the book is self-contained, the story in this book is a continuation to the original trilogy, and it is recommended to read this only after reading the first three books.<br /><br />Mysteries (if any) are very well-maintained, while reading the book until its last page is interesting. Some of the themes mentioned in the book were not new to me, and as a result have not really happened to put me in a state of awe, as a result of which my inability in giving it a perfect five-star rating. However, I was glad to see those embedded themes, and the series' integration with Asimov's other series of his books.<br /><br />Some of my questions which I had conceived while reading the original trilogy were particularly attended to by the author, for which I am glad, such as the question of Earth in the Galactic Empire's History, and the possibility of other life-forms. These concepts have now been well-integrated.<br /><br />Now on to the next in the series: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29582.Foundation_and_Earth__Foundation__5_" title="Foundation and Earth (Foundation #5) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation and Earth</a> :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="700009627211437667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_467019216" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/467019216" />
    <a title="Derek Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1950709-derek-davis"><img alt="Derek Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1289699546p2/1950709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/467019216?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Derek Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Derek Davis" href="/user/show/1950709-derek-davis">Derek Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer467019216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12169149208282109969">I didn't plan to read the "later" Foundation books because most attempts to reinvigorate an early, highly successful series (and except for "Lord of the Rings," no original series of the '50s and '60s was as successful as the Foundation trilogy) usually leave you somewhat embarrassed for the author.<br/><br/>Not here. Rather than trying to reanimate the sword-and-hoopla of much of 1950s SF, Asimov writes us a 450-page logical argument. You might think that would be enough to give Socrates a headache, but,</span>
  <span id="freeText12169149208282109969" style="display:none">I didn't plan to read the "later" Foundation books because most attempts to reinvigorate an early, highly successful series (and except for "Lord of the Rings," no original series of the '50s and '60s was as successful as the Foundation trilogy) usually leave you somewhat embarrassed for the author.<br /><br />Not here. Rather than trying to reanimate the sword-and-hoopla of much of 1950s SF, Asimov writes us a 450-page logical argument. You might think that would be enough to give Socrates a headache, but, as the master storyteller he always was, Asimov keeps you hanging on every unexpected but perfectly reasoned turn of plot.<br /><br />By "logical argument" I mean a warring of intensely bright minds trying to one-up each other's motivations and uncover the structure behind a constantly reorganizing viewpoint of political and social organization. <br /><br />Roughly 200 years after the original stories, the Foundation has taken peaceful control of nearly half the galaxy's million colonized worlds. The Foundation believes that the secretive Second Foundation has been exterminated, but we (of course) know that it still lurks on the former Empire home world of Trantor, controlling the unfolding fate of the galaxy through subtle but benevolent mind-tuning. <br /><br />There's no need to list more facts, because this is not a fact-based novel. It's a constantly unfolding and interfolding of ideas through the truly deft use of mind games. And it works only because Asimov created superb characters who speak to each other not in didactic paragraphs but in a genuine attempt to explain the situation to each other. We, the readers, are but eavesdroppers.<br /><br />One thing from the original series remains the same, and it's always seemed both silly and endearing to me. Despite the fact that the galaxy is home to a quintillion human beings (or, one royal shitload squared), their fate always hangs on tiny a handful of isolated minds, who meet two or three at a time out behind some planet where any two spaceships can always conveniently find each other, like neighborhood rudeboys dreaming up a heist in the parking lot of the Pep Boys' warehouse. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12169149208282109969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3087309679" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3087309679" />
    <a title="Vagabond of Letters, DLitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7531999-vagabond-of-letters-dlitt"><img alt="Vagabond of Letters, DLitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409210541p2/7531999.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3087309679?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vagabond of Letters, DLitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vagabond of Letters, DLitt" href="/user/show/7531999-vagabond-of-letters-dlitt">Vagabond of Letters, DLitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16150025-foundation-s-edge">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3087309679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17692100565178940702">3.25/5<br/><br/>I'm torn on how to rate this book. It isn't like the first three in writing (not least in losing the header references to the Encyclopedia Galactica), which are very terse (Foundation having been serialized) in the fashion of mid-century sci-fi: this is more like modern science fiction, with more of a focus on characters and so on instead of plot, technology, and twist. <br/><br/>The first two novels are relatively harder science fiction. Second Foundation, with the introduction of mentalics, veers </span>
  <span id="freeText17692100565178940702" style="display:none">3.25/5<br /><br />I'm torn on how to rate this book. It isn't like the first three in writing (not least in losing the header references to the Encyclopedia Galactica), which are very terse (Foundation having been serialized) in the fashion of mid-century sci-fi: this is more like modern science fiction, with more of a focus on characters and so on instead of plot, technology, and twist. <br /><br />The first two novels are relatively harder science fiction. Second Foundation, with the introduction of mentalics, veers to the soft. I enjoy Seveneves as much as Star Trek, but the change in tone is jarring. This book continues the shift begun in Second Foundation.<br /><br />It's well-written and gripping for the first two-thirds, but I found the conclusion entirely unsatisfactory. It has something of the Deus ex about it, even though it is nigh as thoroughly hinted as Chekhov's gun.<br /><br />I have been rooting for the Second Foundation for the entire series, ever since I learned it existed. It fits my bookish and mathematical temperament. In the end of this book, the future under the Second Foundation is described as a 'future from calculation, ruled by calculation, a living death'. It sounds like my kind of future. Even the first Foundation, with its machiavellianism, is tolerable: it is just realpolitik. It is described as 'a rebirth of the first Galactic Empire, born in strife and dying in strife': but it is the first Empire born again.<br /><br />Instead we are introduced to Gaia, the Mule's home planet, inhabited by a race of Mules comprising a hive mind - including the natural environment, in a sort of Earth/Animal Liberation Front dream - ruled by the hidden hand of remnant robots left over from the first colonization of the galaxy. I can see why the Mule tried so hard to escape it and its influence after a few pages of description, and almost sympathize with his actions now. (By the way, the description of Gaia in this book doesn't fit at all with what the Mule himself tells about his history, so either the Mule was lying or Gaia is: I think it is likely the latter, Gaia is so creepy.)<br /><br />It gives me strong hints of being a sort of Rousseauvian 'natural' 'paradise' where 'if it feels good, do it' and 'anything goes' and there's no real logic or reason not provided by the robot overlords, but merely a 'good vibing' with everything and anything (aka Hell) - a reflection of our degenerate ethics of late modernity, the inversion of high and low culture, body and social body - as opposed to the appealing ascetic, scholarly self-control of Second Foundationers and their ethic.<br /><br />I digress: in the climax, Gaia and both Foundations are brought to a three-way Mexican standoff, and Trevize (one of the main characters) is, through a bit of Deus ex magic, forced to choose between the three alternate visions for the future: the First Foundation's realpolitik, high technology, and militarism, the Second Foundation's monastic, ascetic scholarship and hidden-hand paternalism, and extending the hive mind of Gaia's 'good vibes' throughout the galaxy to form 'Galaxia'. The decision is entirely predictable as soon as the standoff commences, robbing it of drama and narrative force.<br /><br />Trevize chooses Gaia and Galaxia, both concepts of which are emotionally repulsive to me, especially as contrasted with the adamantine beauty of the Second Foundation. If you are not innately repulsed by the Gaian good-vibes, uninhibited, state-of-nature 'paradise', you'll probably find the ending - and the book - much more to your liking. I'm of the hard Right with libertarian tendencies (like Hans-Hermann Hoppe, but further Right), and Gaianism seems to be the culmination of the collectivist Left's ideals - both the old Marxist Left and the post-70s postmaterial New Left's combined. I'm also very religious, but the scientific materialism of the first trilogy didn't put me off at all, so I don't think it plays a role in my rating here.<br /><br />This choice of the Gaian vision for the future is why the ending is crushingly unsatisfying to me. They're not antiheroes, or evil-is-a-matter-of-perspective types: they are definitely Asimov's good guys, but I find their vision, vibing, and robot paternalism repulsive. I don't often have emotional reactions to fiction books, but boy, did I to this one's conclusion. <br /><br />The two Foundations' memories of Gaia are wiped, and the First Foundation's suspicions of the survival of the Second are allayed. Both Foundations believe they've won a victory.<br /><br />However, Trevize finds out that Gaia (or some other actor) is hiding the existence of Earth - the origin planet - from him, and reveals that he chose the Gaian vision because he was 'temporizing' and believed it could be reversed (though he says he doesn't think it likely he made the wrong decision), whereas the other options would immediately have given either the First or Second Foundations complete hegemony. It is only in this hope that the Gaia/Galaxia plan comes to naught that I read the next book in the series. <br /><br />I hope it comes to naught to redeem the series, for as-is, it has been like listening to a Wagner opera with a hideous screech at the end of the record, which taints the enjoyment of what came before.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17692100565178940702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168814590?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Toby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Toby" href="/user/show/5454475-toby">Toby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385177252" href="/book/show/890555.Foundation_s_Edge">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168814590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10983444777439958621">Expectations are funny things you know. Working in a secondhand bookshop I see so many copies of this title on my heavily discounted shelves all the time, nobody buying it even at $2; I was under the impression that it must've been a very poor addition to the series because every other Asimov gts bought instantly. How wrong I was.<br/><br/>This is quite possibly my favourite of the Foundation novels so far, not including the early robot/Lije Baley books, it would have received 5 stars if it was for the fi</span>
  <span id="freeText10983444777439958621" style="display:none">Expectations are funny things you know. Working in a secondhand bookshop I see so many copies of this title on my heavily discounted shelves all the time, nobody buying it even at $2; I was under the impression that it must've been a very poor addition to the series because every other Asimov gts bought instantly. How wrong I was.<br /><br />This is quite possibly my favourite of the Foundation novels so far, not including the early robot/Lije Baley books, it would have received 5 stars if it was for the final three parts of the story letting it down with its wishy washy 'communing with nature' nonsense. <br /><br />It's quite a bit longer than the original trilogy but Asimov manages to pack the story with intrigue so you barely notice the length. It's fascinating, exciting stuff, taking the series in a whole new direction with new, interesting characters that you can't help but get behind as they each undertake a personal mission that will inevitably draw them all together for an unexpected ending.<br /><br />The 400+ pages fly past, I missed sleep as I couldn't stop myself from starting another part, desperate to know what was going to happen next. The great news is that you don't need to have read the preceding 13 books in the Foundation universe to enjoy this one, the self-contained storyline works completely for once and can be enjoyed by newcomers to the series and old fans alike.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10983444777439958621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1763627005168274399">Way too much time was spend on explaining the theory behind ... Well, everything in the book. This was a good example of way so many people get turned off by sci-fi and think that you can't have entertaining narratives that are scientifically accurate.   <span id="freeText1763627005168274399" style="display:none">Way too much time was spend on explaining the theory behind ... Well, everything in the book. This was a good example of way so many people get turned off by sci-fi and think that you can't have entertaining narratives that are scientifically accurate. Stereotyped, single dimensional characters and don't even get me started on the portrayal of women - in one scene a university professor's wife leaves the dining room because she's offended by the topic of conversation. She said nothing during the entire sequence, only got up and left. Then the men leave the room to continue their conversation so she will be able to come back and clean up the remains of the meal. Ok, maybe if it had been written in the 1950s, but this originally published in the mid 1980s. (Clearly Asimov just ignored the whole women's liberation thing.) In all fairness, there are other female characters that are different. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[One is a mayor and leader of a prominent faction, another is a spy (masquereading as a simple farm woman) for a secret faction and sexy little plaything for heterosexual male fantasies. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But none of them are really even as well developed as the two-dimensional male characters. Oh well, I still have one more of these Foundation books to read. So, I'll keep plugging away at it.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Timothy Freeland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Timothy Freeland" href="/user/show/3797094-timothy-freeland">Timothy Freeland</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer110215675&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110215675" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7281285347906150555">In his fourth installment in the Foundation Series Asimov blunders and completely drops the ball. While the first three novels did a marvelous job of telling the story of The Seldon Plan (The True Main Character of the Foundation Series), Asimov decides to toss what was a very good plot aside in favor of connecting the Foundation Series to the Empire and Robot series. <br/><br/>I was flabbergasted as a dues ex machine arrives to serve only one purpose (make everything fit together). Not only was the sudde</span>
  <span id="freeText7281285347906150555" style="display:none">In his fourth installment in the Foundation Series Asimov blunders and completely drops the ball. While the first three novels did a marvelous job of telling the story of The Seldon Plan (The True Main Character of the Foundation Series), Asimov decides to toss what was a very good plot aside in favor of connecting the Foundation Series to the Empire and Robot series. <br /><br />I was flabbergasted as a dues ex machine arrives to serve only one purpose (make everything fit together). Not only was the sudden twist horrible, it was a giant hole unto itself. The intervention of Gaia would never have been needed if they hadn't interfered in the foundation's existence. <br /><br />Supposedly Gaia calls together the Mayor, the Speaker, Trevise together because without intervention the First Foundation would have gone on conquest and subjugated the Second Foundation or the Second Foundation would have focused on Physical strength and taken a more forceful hand with the First Foundation. None of that would have happened if Gaia had stayed out of the whole event! <br /><br />Think about it: The Mayor wouldn't even have thought to look at Seyshell if Gaia hadn't have orchestrated events to have Trevise go there, and the Second Foundation wouldn't even have had to the inclination to deal with the new physical power of the Foundation if the Gaian's hadn't have, again, revealed themselves to the Second Foundation by interfering with a corrected Seldon Plan. <br /><br />If anything, the Gaian's should have destroyed the mentalic shields of the First Foundation as an apology for destroying the whole Seldon Plan by shrugging of responsibility for The Mule. <br /><br />Terrible. This book was a complete disappointment. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7281285347906150555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
